## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on current population size through density-dependent mechanisms, and may have explicit time dependence through seasonal or environmental changes.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with nonlinear density dependence)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance model)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (flexible asymmetric sigmoid growth)
- Time-dependent Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponential growth with time-varying rate)
- Logistic with time-varying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (seasonal or shifting carrying capacity)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Hassell-type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P)**c2 (contest vs scramble competition)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal logistic growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt proportional to P) → exponential/Malthusian regime indicating density-independent growth
- Quadratic term in P (P - c*P²) → logistic-type density dependence with a carrying capacity, producing sigmoidal population trajectories
- Cubic term in P (P²*(1-cP) or P*(P-a)(K-P)) → Allee effect where very small populations have negative growth rates
- Logarithmic coupling log(c/P)*P → Gompertz-type growth with asymmetric approach to carrying capacity (slow near K, fast at low P)
- Fractional power P**c with 0<c<1 → surface-area-limited growth processes (e.g., nutrient absorption proportional to surface area)
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+cP)) → resource competition saturation where per-capita growth rate decreases smoothly with density
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple critical population thresholds (extinction threshold, carrying capacity)
- Explicit periodic time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) multiplied by growth terms → seasonal or cyclic environmental forcing
- Exponential time factor exp(c*t) modifying parameters → long-term environmental trend such as habitat degradation or improvement
